Prosecco wines for&nbsp=\n; more than 120 years. The winery was founded in 1887 by Francesco Mionetto=\n in the&nbsp; small village of Valdobbiadene, located just north of Venice.=\n On the steep <br /> hillsides of Valdobbiadene, the delicate Prosecco grap=\nes found ideal soil and <br /> climate conditions. At first Francesco bottl=\ned and sold wines to the locals of <br /> the region. He used small casks a=\nnd transported wines by horse and buggy <br /> throughout the town. His bro=\nthers eventually joined him in the business<br />and it became even more es=\ntablished. However, all three brothers were called to serve during WW1 and =\nthe winery was left unattended and sus- tained heavy&nbsp; damage. Eventual=\nly, Francesco&rsquo;s grandsons, Giovanni and Sergio Mionetto, took<br />ov=\ner the winery in 1961 and began re-building.<br /><span></span><br />&nbsp;=\nIn 1982, the Mionetto family introduced autoclave fermentation by&nbsp;swit=\nch- ing to the Charmat method, which allows for better preservation of the&=\nnbsp;flavors and aromas of Prosecco. Prosecco is an especially challenging =\nwine to <br /> produce because of historical ownership laws in the region. =\nWineries&nbsp; traditionally do not own their vineyards or own very little =\nand most Prosecco vineyards are small, ranging in size from only 1-4 hectar=\nes. It is the&nbsp;</font> <font size=3D\"3\">winemaker&rsquo;s job then not =\nonly to produce a high quality sparkling wine, but to&nbsp; maintain the re=\nlationships with local farmers who provide the grapes. Mionetto <br /> is f=\nortunate to have relationships with vineyard owners that date back for&nbsp=\n; generations. Many of the farmers have been working with Mionetto for over=\n 40&nbsp; years. The strength and longevity of these relationships can affe=\nct the quality&nbsp;<br /> and quantity of grapes provided to a winery. Its origin and name can be traced back to&nbsp; the =\ntown of Prosecco in Trieste. Prosecco grapes are transformed into sparkling=\n&nbsp; wine using the Charmat method in which stainless steel tanks and yea=\nst are <br /> utilized to produce a natural second fermentation. The proces=\ns takes&nbsp;approximately 60 days depending on acidity, residual sugar and=\n pressure. table-layout: fixed'><tr>=\n<td valign=3D'top'><div id=3D'950795839466963561-blog' class=3D'blog-body' =\nstyle=3D'float: left;'>=0A<div id=3D'wsite-content'><div id=3D'blog-title'>=\n<a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.html' id=3D'blog-title-=\nlink' class=3D'blog-link'>History of Pumpkin Beer</a> <font id=3D'blog-date=\n'>11/07/2011</font></div><!-- 290500715614243177 -->=0A<div id=3D'blog-comm=\nents'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.html#comments' cl=\nass=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></div><div id=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp; </=\ndiv><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><div  cl=\nass=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><STRONG>The H=\nistory of Pumpkin Beer</STRONG><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>The 20=\n11 season of Pumpkin Ale has proven to be one the most successful seasonal =\nsellers for craft beer makers. The popularity of falls favorite &ldquo;Pump=\nkin Beer&rdquo; has become all the rage. &nbsp;With more than 400 pumpkin b=\neers to choose from today, modern drinkers may not be tasting anything like=\n their beer&rsquo;s colonial ancestors.<br /><span></span><br /><span></spa=\nn>Many would be surprised to discover that Pumpkin Beer has a history in Am=\nerica; its tale goes all the way back to the 1600&rsquo;s with &ldquo;Ameri=\nca&rsquo;s first folk song&rdquo; <br /><span></span><br /><span></span><EM=\n>Instead of pottage and puddings and custards and pies,<br />Our pumpkins a=\nnd parsnips are common supplies;<br />We have pumpkin at morning and pumpki=\nn at noon;<br />If it was not for pumpkins we should be undone<br />&hellip=\n; Hey down, down, hey down derry down&hellip;.<br />If barley be wanting to=\n make into malt<br />We must be contented and think it no fault<br />For we=\n can make liquor, to sweeten our lips,<br />Of pumpkins and parsnips and wa=\nlnut-tree chips.&nbsp; </EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span><EM>~circ=\na 1643</EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>While most Europeans had n=\never even seen a pumpkin, both pumpkins and brown sugar were easily accessi=\nble in early uncolonized America, while proper malt was not. Pumpkin was a =\nnative plant. Colonist brewed pumpkin beer for health and sustenance, repla=\ncing malt entirely with pumpkin meat. <br /><span></span><br /><span></span=\n>Pumpkin beer continued to be a staple through the 18th century but its pop=\nularity began to wane by the early 1900&rsquo;s as the access to quality ma=\nlts became commonplace and the pumpkin itself became viewed as something ru=\nstic and less desirable.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span>Modern pumpki=\nn beers tend to aim for more of a &lsquo;pumpkin pie in a glass&rsquo; appr=\noach as opposed to &lsquo;pumpkin in a glass&rsquo; using spices such a nut=\nmeg and cloves rather than authentic pumpkin flavors. The rebirth of the Pu=\nmpkin beer is credited to <A href=3D\"http://www.buffalobillsbrewery.com/\">B=\nuffalo Bill&rsquo;s Brewery</A> which has been making their America&rsquo;s=\n Original Pumpkin Beer since the late 1980&rsquo;s, using one of George Was=\nhington&rsquo;s recipes as inspiration. &nbsp;Although the experimental bat=\nches used pumpkin as an ingredient, the commercial version stuck with the p=\numpkin pie spice approach instead. <br /><span></span><br /><span></span></=\ndiv>  </div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-item'><a c=\nlass=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twitter.com/share?url=3Dhttp%3=\nA%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F11%2Fhistory-of-pumpkin-beer1.ht=\nml' data-count=3D'horizontal'></a></div><div class=3D'blog-social-item blog=\n-fb-like'><fb:like href=3D'http://suttonwines.com/2/post/2011/11/history-of=\n-pumpkin-beer1.html' show_faces=3D'false' layout=3D'button_count' width=3D'=\n90'></fb:like></div><div style=3D'clear:both'></div></div>=0A<div class=3D'=\nblog-comments-bottom'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.h=\ntml#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>Add Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blog-post=\n-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=0A=0A<div id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/post/201=\n1/07/clown-shoes-hoppy-feet-black-ipa-6-abv.html' id=3D'blog-title-link' cl=\nass=3D'blog-link'>Clown Shoes Hoppy Feet Black IPA 6% ABV</a> <font id=3D'b=\nlog-date'>07/20/2011</font></div><!-- 524253008965367263 -->=0A<div id=3D'b=\nlog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/07/clown-shoes-hoppy-feet-black-ipa-6=\n-abv.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>1 Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blog-=\nseparator'> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'b=\nlog-content'><div  class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: =\nleft; \">Hoppy Feet has been lovingly crafted by combining Premium malt with=\n lots of Amarillo and Columbus Hops. Imperial, or double IPA&rsquo;s are IPA&rsquo;s on s=\nteroids. They&rsquo;re usually 50% stronger and more bitter than normal IPA=\n&rsquo;s. <br /><span></span><br /><span></span> Larry pours a beautiful am=\nber orange with a nice fluffy white head. The first thing you notice is the=\n aroma. Strong hops, grapefruit, pine and floral smells. The taste is spicy=\n, citrusy, piney and hoppy. However, this beer is not just about the hops, =\nit&rsquo;s remarkably well balanced.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span> =\nDouble IPA&rsquo;s are a west coast beer style, but Larry from a brewery in=\n Westminster MA can more than hold it&rsquo;s own against anything from out=\n west.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span></SPAN></div></div><div class=\n=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-item'><a class=3D'twitter-share-=\nbutton' href=3D'http://twitter.com/share?url=3Dhttp%3A%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com=\n%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F03%2Flarryby-dennis.html' data-count=3D'horizontal'></=\na></div><div class=3D'blog-social-item blog-fb-like'><fb:like href=3D'http:=\n//suttonwines.com/2/post/2011/03/larryby-dennis.html' show_faces=3D'false' =\nlayout=3D'button_count' width=3D'90'></fb:like></div><div style=3D'clear:bo=\nth'></div></div>=0A<div class=3D'blog-comments-bottom'><a href=3D'/2/post/2=\n011/03/larryby-dennis.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>Add Comment</a></d=\niv><div id=3D'blog-post-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=0A=0A<div id=3D'blog-title'=\n><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-review-by-dennis.html=\n' id=3D'blog-title-link' class=3D'blog-link'>Jack D'or by Pretty Things    =\n                          Review by Dennis</a> <font id=3D'blog-date'>03/02=\n/2011</font></div><!-- 219831154597403108 -->=0A<div id=3D'blog-comments'><=\na href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-review-by-dennis.html#c=\nomments' class=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></div><div id=3D'blog-separator'=\n> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-conten=\nt'><div  class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><S=\nPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT>Jack Do&rsquo;r i=\ns the first beer from Pretty Things Beer and Ale Project.<SPAN style=3D\"mso=\n-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>It&rsquo;s an American version of the Belgian=\n Saison style.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Saisons were =\nsimple table beers brewed in the winter months for farm workers to enjoy du=\nring the summer.</FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=\n=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000>&nbsp;</FONT></SP=\nAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt=\n\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT>Jack pours a beautiful hazy orange color with=\n a fluffy white head.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Smell =\nis fruity with grape, lemon, apple, grass, and yeast apparent.</FONT></FONT=\n></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE:=\n 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><=\nspan></span>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT=\n>The flavor is close to the aroma, but with a dryness from the three strain=\ns of<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>yeast used during the b=\nrewing.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN></FONT></FONT></SPAN=\n><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\">=\n<FONT color=3D#000000>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></=\nspan>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT>This i=\ns a very complex, very special beer quite possibly like nothing you&rsquo;v=\ne ever tried before.</FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></s=\npan></div></div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-item'>=\n<a class=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twitter.com/share?url=3Dht=\ntp%3A%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F03%2Fjack-dor-by-pretty-thin=\ngs-review-by-dennis.html' data-count=3D'horizontal'></a></div><div class=3D=\n'blog-social-item blog-fb-like'><fb:like href=3D'http://suttonwines.com/2/p=\nost/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-review-by-dennis.html' show_faces=3D'=\nfalse' layout=3D'button_count' width=3D'90'></fb:like></div><div style=3D'c=\nlear:both'></div></div>=0A<div class=3D'blog-comments-bottom'><a href=3D'/2=\n/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-review-by-dennis.html#comments' cla=\nss=3D'blog-link'>Add Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blog-post-separator'>&nbsp=\n;</div>=0A=0A<div id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/youngs-doubl=\ne-chocolate-stout-review-by-dennis.html' id=3D'blog-title-link' class=3D'bl=\nog-link'>Young's Double Chocolate Stout                     Review by Denni=\ns</a> <font id=3D'blog-date'>03/02/2011</font></div><!-- 612875471133224349=\n -->=0A<div id=3D'blog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/youngs-double-c=\nhocolate-stout-review-by-dennis.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>0 Commen=\nts</a></div><div id=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author=\n'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><div  class=3D\"paragraph editable-=\ntext\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT c=\nolor=3D#000000><FONT><FONT size=3D2>Young&rsquo;s Double Chocolate Stout is=\n made in England by Wells &amp; Young&rsquo;s Ltd.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacer=\nun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>This is a sweet, or milk stout style.<SPAN style=3D\"=\nmso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>That means unfermentable sugars are added =\nto the brew kettle to add sweetness and counter the bitterness of the roast=\ned malts.</FONT></FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=\n <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000 size=3D2>&nbsp;</FON=\nT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span> <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 1=\n4pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT><FONT size=3D2>This beer pours a deep beau=\ntiful black color with a nice brown head.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">=\n&nbsp; </SPAN>Aroma is chocolate with hints of coffee.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-sp=\nacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Mouthfeel is rich and creamy.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-=\nspacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>The flavor is what you would expect from the n=\name and more.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Plenty of choc=\nolate flavor, but hints of coffee and roasted malt.</FONT></FONT></FONT></S=\nPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span> <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\">=\n<FONT color=3D#000000 size=3D2>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /=\n><span></span> <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT>=\n<FONT size=3D2>At only 5.2 % alcohol by volume you can easily have a few of=\n these.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>This is a good intro=\nductory beer for someone wanting to try something a little different.<SPAN =\nstyle=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Don&rsquo;t be afraid of the dark=\n!<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </SPAN></FONT></FONT></FONT=\n></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span> <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14=\npt\"><FONT color=3D#000000>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><spa=\nn></span></div></div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-i=\ntem'><a class=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twitter.com/share?url=\n=3Dhttp%3A%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F03%2Fyoungs-double-choc=\nolate-stout-review-by-dennis.html' data-count=3D'horizontal'></a></div><div=\n class=3D'blog-social-item blog-fb-like'><fb:like href=3D'http://suttonwine=\ns.com/2/post/2011/03/youngs-double-chocolate-stout-review-by-dennis.html' s=\nhow_faces=3D'false' layout=3D'button_count' width=3D'90'></fb:like></div><d=\niv style=3D'clear:both'></div></div>=0A<div class=3D'blog-comments-bottom'>=\n<a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/youngs-double-chocolate-stout-review-by-dennis.h=\ntml#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>Add Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blog-post=\n-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=0A=0A<div id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/post/201=\n1/03/first-post.html' id=3D'blog-title-link' class=3D'blog-link'>Welcome to=\n Sutton Wine & Liquors Beer and Wine Review Blog</a> <font id=3D'blog-date'=\n>03/02/2011</font></div><!-- 373401747958382660 -->=0A<div id=3D'blog-comme=\nnts'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/first-post.html#comments' class=3D'blog-lin=\nk'>1 Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-a=\nuthor'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><div  class=3D\"paragraph edit=\nable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><STRONG>The History of Pumpkin Bee=\nr</STRONG><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>The 2011 season of Pumpkin =\nAle has proven to be one the most successful seasonal sellers for craft bee=\nr makers. The popularity of falls favorite &ldquo;Pumpkin Beer&rdquo; has b=\necome all the rage. &nbsp;With more than 400 pumpkin beers to choose from t=\noday, modern drinkers may not be tasting anything like their beer&rsquo;s c=\nolonial ancestors.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span>Many would be surpr=\nised to discover that Pumpkin Beer has a history in America; its tale goes =\nall the way back to the 1600&rsquo;s with &ldquo;America&rsquo;s first folk=\n song&rdquo; <br /><span></span><br /><span></span><EM>Instead of pottage a=\nnd puddings and custards and pies,<br />Our pumpkins and parsnips are commo=\nn supplies;<br />We have pumpkin at morning and pumpkin at noon;<br />If it=\n was not for pumpkins we should be undone<br />&hellip; Hey down, down, hey=\n down derry down&hellip;.<br />If barley be wanting to make into malt<br />=\nWe must be contented and think it no fault<br />For we can make liquor, to =\nsweeten our lips,<br />Of pumpkins and parsnips and walnut-tree chips.&nbsp=\n; </EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span><EM>~circa 1643</EM><br /><spa=\nn></span><br /><span></span>While most Europeans had never even seen a pump=\nkin, both pumpkins and brown sugar were easily accessible in early uncoloni=\nzed America, while proper malt was not. Pumpkin was a native plant. Colonis=\nt brewed pumpkin beer for health and sustenance, replacing malt entirely wi=\nth pumpkin meat. <br /><span></span><br /><span></span>Pumpkin beer continu=\ned to be a staple through the 18th century but its popularity began to wane=\n by the early 1900&rsquo;s as the access to quality malts became commonplac=\ne and the pumpkin itself became viewed as something rustic and less desirab=\nle.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span>Modern pumpkin beers tend to aim f=\nor more of a &lsquo;pumpkin pie in a glass&rsquo; approach as opposed to &l=\nsquo;pumpkin in a glass&rsquo; using spices such a nutmeg and cloves rather=\n than authentic pumpkin flavors. The rebirth of the Pumpkin beer is credite=\nd to <A href=3D\"http://www.buffalobillsbrewery.com/\">Buffalo Bill&rsquo;s B=\nrewery</A> which has been making their America&rsquo;s Original Pumpkin Bee=\nr since the late 1980&rsquo;s, using one of George Washington&rsquo;s recip=\nes as inspiration. &nbsp;Although the experimental batches used pumpkin as =\nan ingredient, the commercial version stuck with the pumpkin pie spice appr=\noach instead. <br /><span></span><br /><span></span></div>  </div><div clas=\ns=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-item'><a     <div id=3D\"nav-bottom\"></div>=0A =\n         <div id=3D\"content-main\">=0A             <div id=3D'wsite-content'=\n class=3D'wsite-not-footer'>=0A<table style=3D'border: 0; width: 100%; tabl=\ne-layout: fixed'><tr><td valign=3D'top'><div id=3D'950795839466963561-blog'=\n class=3D'blog-body' style=3D'float: left;'>=0A<div id=3D'wsite-content'><d=\niv id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.ht=\nml' id=3D'blog-title-link' class=3D'blog-link'>History of Pumpkin Beer</a> =\n<font id=3D'blog-date'>11/07/2011</font></div><!-- 290500715614243177 -->=\n=0A<div id=3D'blog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-=\nbeer1.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></div><div id=3D'blo=\ng-separator'> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><div id=3D=\n'blog-content'><div  class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align=\n: left; \"><STRONG>The History of Pumpkin Beer</STRONG><br /><span></span><b=\nr /><span></span>The 2011 season of Pumpkin Ale has proven to be one the mo=\nst successful seasonal sellers for craft beer makers. The popularity of fal=\nls favorite &ldquo;Pumpkin Beer&rdquo; has become all the rage. &nbsp;With =\nmore than 400 pumpkin beers to choose from today, modern drinkers may not b=\ne tasting anything like their beer&rsquo;s colonial ancestors.<br /><span><=\n/span><br /><span></span>Many would be surprised to discover that Pumpkin B=\neer has a history in America; its tale goes all the way back to the 1600&rs=\nquo;s with &ldquo;America&rsquo;s first folk song&rdquo; <br /><span></span=\n><br /><span></span><EM>Instead of pottage and puddings and custards and pi=\nes,<br />Our pumpkins and parsnips are common supplies;<br />We have pumpki=\nn at morning and pumpkin at noon;<br />If it was not for pumpkins we should=\n be undone<br />&hellip; Hey down, down, hey down derry down&hellip;.<br />=\nIf barley be wanting to make into malt<br />We must be contented and think =\nit no fault<br />For we can make liquor, to sweeten our lips,<br />Of pumpk=\nins and parsnips and walnut-tree chips.&nbsp; </EM><br /><span></span><br /=\n><span></span><EM>~circa 1643</EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>Whi=\nle most Europeans had never even seen a pumpkin, both pumpkins and brown su=\ngar were easily accessible in early uncolonized America, while proper malt =\nwas not. Pumpkin was a native plant. Colonist brewed pumpkin beer for healt=\nh and sustenance, replacing malt entirely with pumpkin meat. <br /><span></=\nspan><br /><span></span>Pumpkin beer continued to be a staple through the 1=\n8th century but its popularity began to wane by the early 1900&rsquo;s as t=\nhe access to quality malts became commonplace and the pumpkin itself became=\n viewed as something rustic and less desirable.<br /><span></span><br /><sp=\nan></span>Modern pumpkin beers tend to aim for more of a &lsquo;pumpkin pie=\n in a glass&rsquo; approach as opposed to &lsquo;pumpkin in a glass&rsquo; =\nusing spices such a nutmeg and cloves rather than authentic pumpkin flavors=\n. The rebirth of the Pumpkin beer is credited to <A href=3D\"http://www.buff=\nalobillsbrewery.com/\">Buffalo Bill&rsquo;s Brewery</A> which has been makin=\ng their America&rsquo;s Original Pumpkin Beer since the late 1980&rsquo;s, =\nusing one of George Washington&rsquo;s recipes as inspiration. &nbsp;Althou=\ngh the experimental batches used pumpkin as an ingredient, the commercial v=\nersion stuck with the pumpkin pie spice approach instead. <br /><span></spa=\nn><br /><span></span></div>  </div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D=\n'blog-social-item'><a class=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twitter=\n.com/share?url=3Dhttp%3A%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F11%2Fhist=\nory-of-pumpkin-beer1.html' data-count=3D'horizontal'></a></div><div class=\n=3D'blog-social-item blog-fb-like'><fb:like href=3D'http://suttonwines.com/=\n2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.html' show_faces=3D'false' layout=\n=3D'button_count' width=3D'90'></fb:like></div><div style=3D'clear:both'></=\ndiv></div>=0A<div class=3D'blog-comments-bottom'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11=\n/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>Add Comment</a=\n></div><div id=3D'blog-post-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=0A=0A<!-- bid: 31250721=\n0719845712 --></div>=0A</div>=0A</td><td class=3D'blog-sidebar' valign=3D't=\nop'><div id=3D'950795839466963561-sidebar' class=3D'column-blog'><div class=\n=3D'blog-sidebar-separator'><ul id=3D'950795839466963561-sidebar-list' clas=\ns=3D'columnlist-blog' style=3D'margin:0; table-layout: fixed'><tr><td valign=3D'top'><div id=3D'950795839466963561=\n-blog' class=3D'blog-body' style=3D'float: left;'>=0A<div id=3D'wsite-conte=\nnt'><div id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/larryby-dennis.html' =\nid=3D'blog-title-link' class=3D'blog-link'>Larry....by Dennis</a> <font id=\n=3D'blog-date'>03/09/2011</font></div><!-- 511416917590115185 -->=0A<div id=\n=3D'blog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/larryby-dennis.html#comments'=\n class=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></div><div id=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp;=\n </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><div =\n class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><SPAN lang=\n=3DEN> Wachusett Larry is an American Imperial IPA. Imperial, or double IPA=\n&rsquo;s are IPA&rsquo;s on steroids. They&rsquo;re usually 50% stronger an=\nd more bitter than normal IPA&rsquo;s. <br /><span></span><br /><span></spa=\nn> Larry pours a beautiful amber orange with a nice fluffy white head. The =\nfirst thing you notice is the aroma. Strong hops, grapefruit, pine and flor=\nal smells. The taste is spicy, citrusy, piney and hoppy. However, this beer=\n is not just about the hops, it&rsquo;s remarkably well balanced.<br /><spa=\nn></span><br /><span></span> Double IPA&rsquo;s are a west coast beer style=\n, but Larry from a brewery in Westminster MA can more than hold it&rsquo;s =\nown against anything from out west.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span></=\nSPAN></div></div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-item'=\n><a class=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twitter.com/share?url=3Dh=\nttp%3A%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F03%2Flarryby-dennis.html' d=\nata-count=3D'horizontal'></a></div><div class=3D'blog-social-item blog-fb-l=\nike'><fb:like href=3D'http://suttonwines.com/2/post/2011/03/larryby-dennis.=\nhtml' show_faces=3D'false' layout=3D'button_count' width=3D'90'></fb:like><=\n/div><div style=3D'clear:both'></div></div>=0A<div class=3D'blog-comments-b=\nottom'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/larryby-dennis.html#comments' class=3D'bl=\nog-link'>Add Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blog-post-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=\n=0A=0A<div id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-=\nthings-review-by-dennis.html' id=3D'blog-title-link' class=3D'blog-link'>Ja=\nck D'or by Pretty Things                              Review by Dennis</a> =\n<font id=3D'blog-date'>03/02/2011</font></div><!-- 219831154597403108 -->=\n=0A<div id=3D'blog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-=\nthings-review-by-dennis.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></=\ndiv><div id=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></=\nb></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><div  class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" st=\nyle=3D\" text-align: left; \"><SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#=\n000000><FONT>Jack Do&rsquo;r is the first beer from Pretty Things Beer and =\nAle Project.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp;     <div id=3D\"nav-bottom\"></div>=0A          <div =\nid=3D\"content-main\">=0A             <div id=3D'wsite-content' class=3D'wsit=\ne-not-footer'>=0A<table style=3D'border: 0; width: 100%; table-layout: fixe=\nd'><tr><td valign=3D'top'><div id=3D'950795839466963561-blog' class=3D'blog=\n-body' style=3D'float: left;'>=0A<div id=3D'wsite-content'><div id=3D'blog-=\ntitle'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.html' id=3D'blog=\n-title-link' class=3D'blog-link'>History of Pumpkin Beer</a> <font id=3D'bl=\nog-date'>11/07/2011</font></div><!-- 290500715614243177 -->=0A<div id=3D'bl=\nog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpkin-beer1.html#comme=\nnts' class=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></div><div id=3D'blog-separator'> &n=\nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><=\ndiv  class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><STRON=\nG>The History of Pumpkin Beer</STRONG><br /><span></span><br /><span></span=\n>The 2011 season of Pumpkin Ale has proven to be one the most successful se=\nasonal sellers for craft beer makers. The popularity of falls favorite &ldq=\nuo;Pumpkin Beer&rdquo; has become all the rage. &nbsp;With more than 400 pu=\nmpkin beers to choose from today, modern drinkers may not be tasting anythi=\nng like their beer&rsquo;s colonial ancestors.<br /><span></span><br /><spa=\nn></span>Many would be surprised to discover that Pumpkin Beer has a histor=\ny in America; its tale goes all the way back to the 1600&rsquo;s with &ldqu=\no;America&rsquo;s first folk song&rdquo; <br /><span></span><br /><span></s=\npan><EM>Instead of pottage and puddings and custards and pies,<br />Our pum=\npkins and parsnips are common supplies;<br />We have pumpkin at morning and=\n pumpkin at noon;<br />If it was not for pumpkins we should be undone<br />=\n&hellip; Hey down, down, hey down derry down&hellip;.<br />If barley be wan=\nting to make into malt<br />We must be contented and think it no fault<br /=\n>For we can make liquor, to sweeten our lips,<br />Of pumpkins and parsnips=\n and walnut-tree chips.&nbsp; </EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span><E=\nM>~circa 1643</EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>While most European=\ns had never even seen a pumpkin, both pumpkins and brown sugar were easily =\naccessible in early uncolonized America, while proper malt was not. Pumpkin=\n was a native plant. Colonist brewed pumpkin beer for health and sustenance=\n, replacing malt entirely with pumpkin meat. <br /><span></span><br /><span=\n></span>Pumpkin beer continued to be a staple through the 18th century but =\nits popularity began to wane by the early 1900&rsquo;s as the access to qua=\nlity malts became commonplace and the pumpkin itself became viewed as somet=\nhing rustic and less desirable.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span>Modern=\n pumpkin beers tend to aim for more of a &lsquo;pumpkin pie in a glass&rsqu=\no; approach as opposed to &lsquo;pumpkin in a glass&rsquo; using spices suc=\nh a nutmeg and cloves rather than authentic pumpkin flavors. The rebirth of=\n the Pumpkin beer is credited to <A href=3D\"http://www.buffalobillsbrewery.=\ncom/\">Buffalo Bill&rsquo;s Brewery</A> which has been making their America&=\nrsquo;s Original Pumpkin Beer since the late 1980&rsquo;s, using one of Geo=\nrge Washington&rsquo;s recipes as inspiration. &nbsp;Although the experimen=\ntal batches used pumpkin as an ingredient, the commercial version stuck wit=\nh the pumpkin pie spice approach instead. <br /><span></span><br /><span></=\nspan></div>  </div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-ite=\nm'><a class=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twitter.com/share?url=\n=3Dhttp%3A%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F11%2Fhistory-of-pumpkin=\n-beer1.html' data-count=3D'horizontal'></a></div><div class=3D'blog-social-=\nitem blog-fb-like'><fb:like href=3D'http://suttonwines.com/2/post/2011/11/h=\nistory-of-pumpkin-beer1.html' show_faces=3D'false' layout=3D'button_count' =\nwidth=3D'90'></fb:like></div><div style=3D'clear:both'></div></div>=0A<div =\nclass=3D'blog-comments-bottom'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/11/history-of-pumpki=\nn-beer1.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>Add Comment</a></div><div id=3D'=\nblog-post-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=0A=0A<div id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2=\n/post/2011/07/clown-shoes-hoppy-feet-black-ipa-6-abv.html' id=3D'blog-title=\n-link' class=3D'blog-link'>Clown Shoes Hoppy Feet Black IPA 6% ABV</a> <fon=\nt id=3D'blog-date'>07/20/2011</font></div><!-- 524253008965367263 -->=0A<di=\nv id=3D'blog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/07/clown-shoes-hoppy-feet-bl=\nack-ipa-6-abv.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>1 Comment</a></div><div id=\n=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><di=\nv id=3D'blog-content'><div  class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" tex=\nt-align: left; \">Hoppy Feet has been lovingly crafted by combining Premium =\nmalt with lots of Amarillo and Columbus Hops. <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><div  class=\n=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><SPAN lang=3DEN>=\n Wachusett Larry is an American Imperial IPA. Imperial, or double IPA&rsquo=\n;s are IPA&rsquo;s on steroids. They&rsquo;re usually 50% stronger and more=\n bitter than normal IPA&rsquo;s. <br /><span></span><br /><span></span> Lar=\nry pours a beautiful amber orange with a nice fluffy white head. The first =\nthing you notice is the aroma. Strong hops, grapefruit, pine and floral sme=\nlls. The taste is spicy, citrusy, piney and hoppy. However, this beer is no=\nt just about the hops, it&rsquo;s remarkably well balanced.<br /><span></sp=\nan><br /><span></span> Double IPA&rsquo;s are a west coast beer style, but =\nLarry from a brewery in Westminster MA can more than hold it&rsquo;s own ag=\nainst anything from out west.<br /><span></span><br /><span></span></SPAN><=\n/div></div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div class=3D'blog-social-item'><a cl=\nass=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twitter.com/share?url=3Dhttp%3A=\n%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F03%2Flarryby-dennis.html' data-co=\nunt=3D'horizontal'></a></div><div class=3D'blog-social-item blog-fb-like'><=\nfb:like href=3D'http://suttonwines.com/2/post/2011/03/larryby-dennis.html' =\nshow_faces=3D'false' layout=3D'button_count' width=3D'90'></fb:like></div><=\ndiv style=3D'clear:both'></div></div>=0A<div class=3D'blog-comments-bottom'=\n><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/larryby-dennis.html#comments' class=3D'blog-lin=\nk'>Add Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blog-post-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=0A=0A<=\ndiv id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-=\nreview-by-dennis.html' id=3D'blog-title-link' class=3D'blog-link'>Jack D'or=\n by Pretty Things                              Review by Dennis</a> <font i=\nd=3D'blog-date'>03/02/2011</font></div><!-- 219831154597403108 -->=0A<div i=\nd=3D'blog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-re=\nview-by-dennis.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></div><div =\nid=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp; </div><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><=\ndiv id=3D'blog-content'><div  class=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" t=\next-align: left; \"><SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><F=\nONT>Jack Do&rsquo;r is the first beer from Pretty Things Beer and Ale Proje=\nct.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>It&rsquo;s an American v=\nersion of the Belgian Saison style.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp;=\n </SPAN>Saisons were simple table beers brewed in the winter months for far=\nm workers to enjoy during the summer.</FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></spa=\nn><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000=\n000>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN sty=\nle=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT>Jack pours a beautiful h=\nazy orange color with a fluffy white head.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\"=\n>&nbsp; </SPAN>Smell is fruity with grape, lemon, apple, grass, and yeast a=\npparent.</FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPA=\nN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /=\n><span></span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT =\ncolor=3D#000000><FONT>The flavor is close to the aroma, but with a dryness =\nfrom the three strains of<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>ye=\nast used during the brewing.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN=\n></FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN style=\n=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /><span>=\n</span><br /><span></span>=0D <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=\n=3D#000000><FONT>This is a very complex, very special beer quite possibly l=\nike nothing you&rsquo;ve ever tried before.</FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span=\n></span><br /><span></span></div></div><div class=3D'blog-social'><div clas=\ns=3D'blog-social-item'><a class=3D'twitter-share-button' href=3D'http://twi=\ntter.com/share?url=3Dhttp%3A%2F%2Fsuttonwines.com%2F2%2Fpost%2F2011%2F03%2F=\njack-dor-by-pretty-things-review-by-dennis.html' data-count=3D'horizontal'>=\n</a></div><div class=3D'blog-social-item blog-fb-like'><fb:like href=3D'htt=\np://suttonwines.com/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-review-by-denn=\nis.html' show_faces=3D'false' layout=3D'button_count' width=3D'90'></fb:lik=\ne></div><div style=3D'clear:both'></div></div>=0A<div class=3D'blog-comment=\ns-bottom'><a href=3D'/2/post/2011/03/jack-dor-by-pretty-things-review-by-de=\nnnis.html#comments' class=3D'blog-link'>Add Comment</a></div><div id=3D'blo=\ng-post-separator'>&nbsp;</div>=0A=0A<div id=3D'blog-title'><a href=3D'/2/po=\nst/2011/03/youngs-double-chocolate-stout-review-by-dennis.html' id=3D'blog-=\ntitle-link' class=3D'blog-link'>Young's Double Chocolate Stout             =\n        Review by Dennis</a> <font id=3D'blog-date'>03/02/2011</font></div>=\n<!-- 612875471133224349 -->=0A<div id=3D'blog-comments'><a href=3D'/2/post/=\n2011/03/youngs-double-chocolate-stout-review-by-dennis.html#comments' class=\n=3D'blog-link'>0 Comments</a></div><div id=3D'blog-separator'> &nbsp; </div=\n><div id=3D'blog-author'> <b></b></div><div id=3D'blog-content'><div  class=\n=3D\"paragraph editable-text\" style=3D\" text-align: left; \"><SPAN style=3D\"F=\nONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT><FONT size=3D2>Young&rsquo;s Do=\nuble Chocolate Stout is made in England by Wells &amp; Young&rsquo;s Ltd.<S=\nPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>This is a sweet, or milk stou=\nt style.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>That means unfermen=\ntable sugars are added to the brew kettle to add sweetness and counter the =\nbitterness of the roasted malts.</FONT></FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></s=\npan><br /><span></span> <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#0000=\n00 size=3D2>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span> <SPA=\nN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000><FONT><FONT size=3D2>This=\n beer pours a deep beautiful black color with a nice brown head.<SPAN style=\n=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Aroma is chocolate with hints of coffe=\ne.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Mouthfeel is rich and cre=\namy.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>The flavor is what you =\nwould expect from the name and more.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp=\n; </SPAN>Plenty of chocolate flavor, but hints of coffee and roasted malt.<=\n/FONT></FONT></FONT></SPAN><br /><span></span><br /><span></span> <SPAN sty=\nle=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT color=3D#000000 size=3D2>&nbsp;</FONT></SPAN><=\nbr /><span></span><br /><span></span> <SPAN style=3D\"FONT-SIZE: 14pt\"><FONT=\n color=3D#000000><FONT><FONT size=3D2>At only 5.2 % alcohol by volume you c=\nan easily have a few of these.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SP=\nAN>This is a good introductory beer for someone wanting to try something a =\nlittle different.<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp; </SPAN>Don&rsquo;=\nt be afraid of the dark!<SPAN style=3D\"mso-spacerun: yes\">&nbsp;&nbsp; The popularity of falls favorite &ldquo;=\nPumpkin Beer&rdquo; has become all the rage. &nbsp;With more than 400 pumpk=\nin beers to choose from today, modern drinkers may not be tasting anything =\nlike their beer&rsquo;s colonial ancestors.<br /><span></span><br /><span><=\n/span>Many would be surprised to discover that Pumpkin Beer has a history i=\nn America; its tale goes all the way back to the 1600&rsquo;s with &ldquo;A=\nmerica&rsquo;s first folk song&rdquo; <br /><span></span><br /><span></span=\n><EM>Instead of pottage and puddings and custards and pies,<br />Our pumpki=\nns and parsnips are common supplies;<br />We have pumpkin at morning and pu=\nmpkin at noon;<br />If it was not for pumpkins we should be undone<br />&he=\nllip; Hey down, down, hey down derry down&hellip;.<br />If barley be wantin=\ng to make into malt<br />We must be contented and think it no fault<br />Fo=\nr we can make liquor, to sweeten our lips,<br />Of pumpkins and parsnips an=\nd walnut-tree chips.&nbsp; </EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span><EM>~=\ncirca 1643</EM><br /><span></span><br /><span></span>While most Europeans h=\nad never even seen a pumpkin, both pumpkins and brown sugar were easily acc=\nessible in early uncolonized America, while proper malt was not. Pumpkin wa=\ns a native plant.
